  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_1f66f17c-9748-455f-b013-536571537caa'
      });

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer10396717381304332785"><i>A Long Walk to Water</i> begins as two stories, told in alternating sections, about a girl in Sudan in 2008 and a boy in Sudan in 1985. The girl, Nya, is fetching water from a pond that is two hours’ walk from her home: she makes two trips to the pond every day. The boy, Salva, becomes one of the "lost boys" of Sudan, refugees who cover the African continent on foot as they se</span>
  <span id="freeText10396717381304332785" style="display:none"><i>A Long Walk to Water</i> begins as two stories, told in alternating sections, about a girl in Sudan in 2008 and a boy in Sudan in 1985. The girl, Nya, is fetching water from a pond that is two hours’ walk from her home: she makes two trips to the pond every day. The boy, Salva, becomes one of the "lost boys" of Sudan, refugees who cover the African continent on foot as they search for their families and for a safe place to stay. Enduring every hardship from loneliness to attack by armed rebels to contact with killer lions and crocodiles, Salva is a survivor, and his story goes on to intersect with Nya’s in an astonishing and moving way.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10396717381304332785" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/595957-i-m-going-to-do-a-summer-book-group-for">I&#39;m going to do a summer book group for just three months. The theme is Africa. We are going to read, &quot;A long walk to water&quot;, &quot;Listening for lions&quot;, and I need one more. Any thoughts? It needs to be a fairly short and easy read. I&#39;ve started &quot;Americanah&quot; but think it will be too long. These are busy moms short on time.</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_595957'><a id="like_count_community_question_595957" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/595957?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">7 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F7981456-a-long-walk-to-water">like</a></span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/33230497-gay-lynn"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1405911373i/33230497._UX100_CR0,8,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/33230497-gay-lynn">Gay Lynn</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">How about several picture books? Or just let different ones read different books. <br/>* Beatrice's Goat which is emblematic for Heifer's International's w<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">How about several picture books? Or just let different ones read different books. <br />* Beatrice's Goat which is emblematic for Heifer's International's work would be wonderful. True Story. Parenthetically many other NGO's now give gifts similar to the effective Heifer model...<br />**I love the message of Fly, Eagle, Fly!By Christopher Gregorowski--kind of a fable with great illustrations. This South African tale might start discussion.<br />***Mufaro's Beautiful Daughters By John Steptoe is somewhat an African Cinderella story. It's in all school libraries, most would have read it already. Also beautifully illustrated.<br />****Galimoto" by Karen Williams may not be about an actual child but children in general in Malawi and many countries contriving their own toys. I've seen toys sold in markets in Africa and sold in Fair Trade stores which sell products to American with less going to the middle man. One in my town is Sojourns in Birmingham AL There are many. Not all have toys, but the stores are there. www dot worldcrafts dot org<br />*****Wangari's Trees of Peace: A True Story from Africa –by Jeanette Winter is a true story of a poor farming lady who hated the deforestation of Kenya and brought change to her country. She won a Nobel Prize I believe for her work.<br />(I like MomToKippy's idea of Number 1 Detective Agency. They are a bit slow reading for me, but fun. Simple detective work and a little budding romance for a lady trying to decide if she's settling for the guy who cares for her. PBS showed BBC renditions of the books. The shows are at my library in the DVD section. )<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

<div id="review_1816780379" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1816780379" />
    <a title="Mischenko" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1194517-mischenko"><img alt="Mischenko" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587209348p2/1194517.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1816780379?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mischenko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mischenko" href="/user/show/1194517-mischenko">Mischenko</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780547577319" href="/book/show/10386845-a-long-walk-to-water">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1816780379" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7507462662335856050"><i>A Long Walk to Water</i> by Linda Sue Park is based on the true story of Salva Dut, one of the Lost Boys from Sudan during the second Sudanese Civil War in 1985. The book also includes a separate narrative about a girl named Nya, which takes place in Sudan as well, but beginning in 2008. Throughout the book we learn about Nya and Salva’s circumstances and their struggles.<br/><br/>Salva’s story is harrowing. It’s during a normal school day in 1985 that shots are heard–the war has arrived in his village–and he</span>
  <span id="freeText7507462662335856050" style="display:none"><i>A Long Walk to Water</i> by Linda Sue Park is based on the true story of Salva Dut, one of the Lost Boys from Sudan during the second Sudanese Civil War in 1985. The book also includes a separate narrative about a girl named Nya, which takes place in Sudan as well, but beginning in 2008. Throughout the book we learn about Nya and Salva’s circumstances and their struggles.<br /><br />Salva’s story is harrowing. It’s during a normal school day in 1985 that shots are heard–the war has arrived in his village–and he’s forced to run into the bush for safety.<br /><br /><i>“Go quickly, all of you,” the teacher said, his voice low and urgent. “Into the bush. Do you hear me? Not home. Don’t run home. They will be going into the villages. Stay away from villages–run into the bush.”</i><br /><br />He has no idea where he’s going; he only knows he must seek safety as far away from home as possible. Traveling with different groups of people, Salva is scared and surrounded by danger; there’s barely any food or water and he faces dangerous wild animals, the sweltering heat, and soldiers armed with guns. It’s hard to imagine the fear he must’ve felt being a child amongst strangers, separated from his family, and now in the wilderness. Years go by as he travels, settling into multiple refugee camps. Salva witnesses much death and wonders if he’ll ever find his family again.<br /><br />Nya’s story begins in 2008 as she and her family struggles to locate fresh water. Nya spends most of the day traveling back and forth in the scorching heat to a pond to fetch water for her family. Members of her family and others have actually been sick from drinking contaminated water. Life is challenging without access to clean water and rather than go to school like other children her age, Nya has to spend most of her days just fetching water without much time for anything else. One day, Nya learns that something good is finally coming to their village: a new water well.<br /><br />Honestly, I don’t remember hearing about Salva’s story before now. I ended up reading this book with my kids for their reading discussion group. We all loved the book, even though it’s frightening and even hard to read in a few parts. The book is written well, and what a page turner it is. The author did such a wonderful job weaving these two narratives together. We couldn’t put it down and kept asking ourselves: <i>What’s going to happen to Salva? Is his family alive? How are these stories connected?</i> Along with the two narratives, you also learn about the history of Sudan, the different tribes, a bit of culture, and their consistent struggle for clean water. It’s odd the things we humans take for granted. I honestly don’t think I’ll ever look at a glass of water the same again. By the end of the story I was in tears. This book is incredibly moving with a strong message for any age. It’s truly a book I recommend to everyone.<br /><br /><i>“Stay calm when things are hard or not going right with you. You will get through it when you persevere instead of quitting. Quitting leads to much less happiness in life than perseverance and hope.”</i> –Salva Dut<br /><br />I don’t want to spoil anything, but the extras at the end of the story had us doing research online afterward to learn more.<br /><br />If you’d like to learn more about the Water for South Sudan project, you can find it at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.waterforsouthsudan.org">https://www.waterforsouthsudan.org</a><br /><br />You can also read this review @<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://readrantrockandroll.com/2019/03/12/book-review-a-long-walk-to-water-by-linda-sue-park-bookreview-alongwalktowater-middlegradebooks/">https://readrantrockandroll.com/2019/...</a><br /><br />Age Range: 10 – 12 years<br />Grade Level: 5 – 7<br />Paperback: 128 pages<br />Publisher: HMH Books for Young Readers; Reprint edition (October 4, 2011)<br />Language: English<br />ISBN-10: 0547577311<br />ISBN-13: 978-0547577319</span>
  <a data-text-id="7507462662335856050" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1500011618" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1500011618" />
    <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader"><img alt="Aj the Ravenous Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557800982p2/30248594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1500011618?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aj the Ravenous Reader" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader">Aj the Ravenous Reader</a>

    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Aj the Ravenous Reader by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/28891877-darina">Darina</a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=emotionally-intense">emotionally-intense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=reality-bites">reality-bites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=five-stars">five-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=unexpectedly-good">unexpectedly-good</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1500011618" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10013686687110913082"><br/><b> <i> “I need only to get through the rest of this day. This day and no other.” </i></b> <br/><br/>Where there is a child, there is always joy. I always thought this was true but the story told otherwise. This is a true to life story of Salva, an 11 year old boy who found little to almost no place in a world where people struggle to survive an almost endless series of conflicts during the Second Sudanese Civil War that started in 1983 . <br/><br/>To adults caught in a tumultuous succession of life threatening obstacles, Salva </span>
  <span id="freeText10013686687110913082" style="display:none"><br /><b> <i> “I need only to get through the rest of this day. This day and no other.” </i></b> <br /><br />Where there is a child, there is always joy. I always thought this was true but the story told otherwise. This is a true to life story of Salva, an 11 year old boy who found little to almost no place in a world where people struggle to survive an almost endless series of conflicts during the Second Sudanese Civil War that started in 1983 . <br /><br />To adults caught in a tumultuous succession of life threatening obstacles, Salva is a burden, someone who will only slow them down, just another mouth to feed. <b>*sniffs*</b> It’s unbelievable where the young boy found all that courage and will to live. Of the many things I’ve learned from him, it is to cling to hope the wisest possible way that hit me the most.<br /><br /><b>
  <i> “He tried not to lose hope. At the same time, he tried not to hope too much.” </i>
</b><br /><br />Written in a lyrical narrative but easy and timeless style of language allowing the reader to feel more, the story completely seized my heart. The vivid, wistful recollections of the young boy’s perilous journey by foot from Sudan to Ethiopia then later to Kenya were plainly told, nothing very emotional. In fact, the writing style seems to be even a bit dismissive of tragic events as if in a <b>life-sucks-but-hurry-up-and-move-on-now approach</b> but it still brought me to puddles of tears. It’s an inspirational piece of literature that is definitely worth your time.<br /><br />Thank you to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/28891877-darina" rel="nofollow noopener">Shanna/Darina</a> for bringing this book to my attention. I had no idea this ever existed before I stalked your profile and of course, I didn’t forget. <b>HAPPY BIRTHDAY, MY DEAR FRIEND! WISHING YOU A SPECIAL DAY, GOOD HEALTH, HAPPINESS AND MORE GREAT BOOKS TO READ! &lt;3 </b><br /><br /> <br /></span>

<div id="review_193325832" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/193325832" />
    <a title="Judith Weaver" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4082298-judith-weaver"><img alt="Judith Weaver" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530909460p2/4082298.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/193325832?book_show_action=true">Aug 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Judith Weaver" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Judith Weaver" href="/user/show/4082298-judith-weaver">Judith Weaver</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">grades 5 and up</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer193325832" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14924166781755799660">Quick read good for multiple ability levels.This book should be an easy inclusion into 7th grade Geography, 6th grade world history, or as an addition to a Holocaust unit. This is how I plan to use it with my 7th grade reading teacher. For younger readers, this book may encourage a class to adopt a project to help bring water to children their age in other places in the world.<br/><br/>Book is told from two viewpoints. One is a girl walking each day to get the water her family needs which she carries home</span>
  <span id="freeText14924166781755799660" style="display:none">Quick read good for multiple ability levels.This book should be an easy inclusion into 7th grade Geography, 6th grade world history, or as an addition to a Holocaust unit. This is how I plan to use it with my 7th grade reading teacher. For younger readers, this book may encourage a class to adopt a project to help bring water to children their age in other places in the world.<br /><br />Book is told from two viewpoints. One is a girl walking each day to get the water her family needs which she carries home in plastic gallon jugs. The trip takes her all day and while not mentioned in the story, this could be a dangerous trip for her. The second viewpoint is from a boy in the 80's who is at school when his village is attacked. He runs into the woods and that is the last of his childhood of living with family or a village. He is in fact one of the Lost Boys. <br /><br />The two stories come together in an upbeat ending meant to inspire the reader to make a better world.<br /><br />Parks intended this book for children to read, so there is not the terror or violence that this book could contain. It does contain some difficult situations -- a boy carried off by a lion in the night, the burning of a village, etc. <br /><br />I would read this book before handing it to a student younger than 6th grade. <br /><br />One more comment, because the book ends with an addendum about an elementary school putting a well in the girl's village, students may want to initiate a project like the one in the book. Be careful if you do this with the kids, so that your money really goes to putting in a well, and not in some warlord's pocket. Rotary does projects like this -- and others of course -- and that might be the way to go.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14924166781755799660" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2047291789" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2047291789" />

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="BernLuvsBooks " class="user" itemprop="url" name="BernLuvsBooks " href="/user/show/3087404-bernluvsbooks">BernLuvsBooks </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3087404-bernluvsbooks?shelf=just-for-tweens-middle-grade">just-for-tweens-middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3087404-bernluvsbooks?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3087404-bernluvsbooks?shelf=fave-reads">fave-reads</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2047291789" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1301223638324039177"><b> A Long Walk to Water was a poignant, touching story that will appeal to readers of all ages. </b><br/><br/>While technically a middle grade novel, this is a story that everyone would benefit from reading. It's a quick read, told as two alternating stories - that of a young girl Nya in the Sudan in 2008 and a young man Salva in 1985. <b> Both of their stories are compelling, emotional and inspirational. </b><br/><br/>Nya must walk hours each day to a far away well to get water for her family. Salva's story is heart-wrenching.</span>
  <span id="freeText1301223638324039177" style="display:none"><b> A Long Walk to Water was a poignant, touching story that will appeal to readers of all ages. </b><br /><br />While technically a middle grade novel, this is a story that everyone would benefit from reading. It's a quick read, told as two alternating stories - that of a young girl Nya in the Sudan in 2008 and a young man Salva in 1985. <b> Both of their stories are compelling, emotional and inspirational. </b><br /><br />Nya must walk hours each day to a far away well to get water for her family. Salva's story is heart-wrenching. His village is attacked and he is separated from his family. Salva's journey is fraught with loss, tragedy, unwavering hope and courage. It was unimaginable to me to think about the horrors children face when they are displaced from their homes, separated from their families and in refugee camps. Salva's sheer will to survive was inspirational. I don't know how I'd cope in such a situation. <br /><br />I loved how these two seemingly unconnected stories intertwined in the end. What the book lacks in pages it makes up for in impact. It is impossible not to feel empathy for the characters within these pages and be moved by their stories. <b> This is one book I highly recommend reading &amp; discussing with all the important children in your life. </b></span>
  <a data-text-id="1301223638324039177" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_180077487" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/180077487" />
    <a title="Heidi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3904308-heidi"><img alt="Heidi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1463892304p2/3904308.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/180077487?book_show_action=true">Jun 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heidi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heidi" href="/user/show/3904308-heidi">Heidi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer180077487" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7022193166741784835">There are some stories that need to be told regardless of how sad or horrifying they might be. The challenge becomes even harder when the stories are being told to children. How much should one include? What details are necessary and what can be left out without changing the story too much? And what about stories that involve extreme violence and severe suffering? How best to tell the story? These questions can be debated over and over again because there is no one right answer. No two authors w</span>
  <span id="freeText7022193166741784835" style="display:none">There are some stories that need to be told regardless of how sad or horrifying they might be. The challenge becomes even harder when the stories are being told to children. How much should one include? What details are necessary and what can be left out without changing the story too much? And what about stories that involve extreme violence and severe suffering? How best to tell the story? These questions can be debated over and over again because there is no one right answer. No two authors will present the same story in the same way. <br /><br />This book follows two main characters, Nya, a child living in Southern Sudan, who must spend every day walking to and from a pond bringing water to her family, and Salva, who twenty-three years earlier became a refugee when his village was attacked by soldiers from the north. The story about Salva is the longer of the two and follows the eleven-year-old as he runs from his school and must somehow cross hundreds of miles of desert, swamp, and forest to reach safety. After six years in the refugee camp, Salva faces terror once again as the Ethiopian soldiers force all the Sudanese refugees back into Sudan, killing hundreds in the process. But Salva finds the strength and hope to survive and becomes a leader among what has become known as the Lost Boys of the Sudan. These boys were orphans who struggled to survive on their own. Some of these boys were able to find a way to not only survive, but to help those left behind. Salva's story intersects with Nya's in an interesting way, showing that the efforts of one can have a far-reaching effect.<br /><br />While the book does explain some of the horrors that the Lost Children of the Sudan and the other refugees faced, it does not do so in a graphic way, and the story is not about despair or violence, it's about hope, which makes the book great to share with students who face their own challenges. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7022193166741784835" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2848246072" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2848246072" />
    <a title="David Schaafsma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/269235-david-schaafsma"><img alt="David Schaafsma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574997804p2/269235.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781936223121" href="/book/show/8735822-a-long-walk-to-water">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/269235-david-schaafsma?shelf=middle-grades">middle-grades</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/269235-david-schaafsma?shelf=environment">environment</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/269235-david-schaafsma?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/269235-david-schaafsma?shelf=immigration">immigration</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2848246072" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2955064730402513007">I was looking for a kid book on the environment and knew children's book author Linda Sue Park had (in 2002) won an award for A Single Shard, and though I knew nothing about this book (rated more than 48K on Goodreads, yay!) I listened to it in a little over two hours. For a book this short it probably crams too much information for middle grades kids to easily digest, but they can do classroom (or home!) research on it, too. <br/><br/>There are two parallel stories, both of them based on extensive interv</span>
  <span id="freeText2955064730402513007" style="display:none">I was looking for a kid book on the environment and knew children's book author Linda Sue Park had (in 2002) won an award for A Single Shard, and though I knew nothing about this book (rated more than 48K on Goodreads, yay!) I listened to it in a little over two hours. For a book this short it probably crams too much information for middle grades kids to easily digest, but they can do classroom (or home!) research on it, too. <br /><br />There are two parallel stories, both of them based on extensive interviews and research, one of a boy Salva Dut, one of the Lost Boys from the second Sudanese Civil War in 1985, and a girl, Nya, in 2008. We get a pretty fast version of the growing up story of Salva, who is separated form his family, lives for years in refugee camps and is lucky to be chosen to come to the US to live. Nya has to walk two times a day many miles to get water for her family, as resources are quickly (and literally) evaporating (as with many places on the planet).<br /><br />It's a powerful story about war, water, refugees, a genocide, courage, and a little bit of hope. Salva speaks in the end about a Sudanese project he sets up involving wells that kids/families could get involved in. That Salva and Nya's stories link in the end is a cool thing here. Terrible, horrific things happened and still happen in Sudan, but it's an important story to hear about, told simply and as a model from Park about socially committed research that young people and adults can take a deeper dive into.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2955064730402513007" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2160448057" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2160448057" />

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2160448057" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer1578143383818867861">After reading this book, I felt like my heart was pierced by an arrow, right in the center, bulls-eye. The story was sad, but in the end, it was a happy ending. There was one part that I thought was most heartbreaking. If you read this book, you might remember. It was the part when Salva's uncle getting shot by the burglars, by his own gun in the desert. And the most irritating part is that they laughed... they laughed! They just killed someone! In the beginning, I thought it was inhuman. But af</span>
  <span id="freeText1578143383818867861" style="display:none">After reading this book, I felt like my heart was pierced by an arrow, right in the center, bulls-eye. The story was sad, but in the end, it was a happy ending. There was one part that I thought was most heartbreaking. If you read this book, you might remember. It was the part when Salva's uncle getting shot by the burglars, by his own gun in the desert. And the most irritating part is that they laughed... they laughed! They just killed someone! In the beginning, I thought it was inhuman. But after I got to know a little about the history and culture of Sudan, I learned that it was "normal". I became "heart-repaired" in the end because, in the beginning, all the way to the end, it was mostly sad and fist clenching stories. Nya's tiring life. Salva's life-threatening story. In the end, as you might know, the two meet, young Nya, and grown-up Salva. Nya gets to go to school, because of the well that Salva and his crew dug (I won't give more and specific details of the story because I am not a spoiler). I guess this can be a happy ending. Read this yourself, I really enjoyed it. I recommend this book to all people, except very sensitive and very easily impressed, very easily heart-struck, or very easily moved. This is because these type of people might start crying in the middle of this book!<br />I can't connect to this story at all. I just can't. These type of "true" stories are just too rare, but in the end, it might be common to some people. I wish others can read this book so that they have a similar thinking as me, and actually try to help types of people such as Nya and Salva. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1578143383818867861" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/114928230?book_show_action=true">Aug 02, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Krista the Krazy Kataloguer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Krista the Krazy Kataloguer" href="/user/show/316102-krista-the-krazy-kataloguer">Krista the Krazy Kataloguer</a>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/316102-krista-the-krazy-kataloguer?shelf=read-historical-fiction">read-historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/316102-krista-the-krazy-kataloguer?shelf=read-iic">read-iic</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/316102-krista-the-krazy-kataloguer?shelf=read-jane-addams-award">read-jane-addams-award</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer114928230" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3243305104722830529">This novel is divided into two alternating narratives that come together in the end. In brown print is the story, set in 2008, of Nya, a young girl from Sudan who has to walk 8 hours round trip to fetch water every day, twice a day. In black print is the story of Salva, a young Sudanese boy whose village is attacked by the rebels in 1985 and who ends up fleeing across the desert to a refugee camp in Ethiopia. After witnessing many horrors, he and other "lost boys," homeless and orphaned, walk ba</span>
  <span id="freeText3243305104722830529" style="display:none">This novel is divided into two alternating narratives that come together in the end. In brown print is the story, set in 2008, of Nya, a young girl from Sudan who has to walk 8 hours round trip to fetch water every day, twice a day. In black print is the story of Salva, a young Sudanese boy whose village is attacked by the rebels in 1985 and who ends up fleeing across the desert to a refugee camp in Ethiopia. After witnessing many horrors, he and other "lost boys," homeless and orphaned, walk back across Sudan to refugee camps in Kenya. Salva's story takes place from 1985, when he is eleven, until his path crosses with Nya's in 2009. It is based on the true story of a man whom the author knows, the real Salva Dut, who eventually was flown to Rochester, New York, to begin his life anew. How does Salva come to meet Nya? Read and find out! Salva's story is both heartbreaking and heartwarming, as the reader laments that children should have to experience such terrible things and also marvels that a child could be so courageous. Highly recommended, especially combined with Mary Williams' <i>Brothers in Hope: the Story of the Lost Boys of Sudan</i>, Alice Mead's <i>Year of No Rain</i>, and Katherine Applegate's <i>Home of the Brave</i>. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3243305104722830529" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_527600994" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/527600994?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cheryl" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cheryl" href="/user/show/11255849-cheryl">Cheryl</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/10943812-a-long-walk-to-water">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11255849-cheryl?shelf=africa">africa</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer527600994" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18289041240529071694">You should start by first knowing that the book is a children's book--otherwise the writing style will be off-putting. It is a heart-wrenching story of a boy (Salva) who is separated from his parents during the religious war between Arab-Africans and Africans in Sudan. He joins a group and they first try to make their way to Ethiopia where they are chased off by soldiers and forced to jump into a lake filled with crocodiles. He then spends a year and a half with a group headed for Kenya--then Am</span>
  <span id="freeText18289041240529071694" style="display:none">You should start by first knowing that the book is a children's book--otherwise the writing style will be off-putting. It is a heart-wrenching story of a boy (Salva) who is separated from his parents during the religious war between Arab-Africans and Africans in Sudan. He joins a group and they first try to make their way to Ethiopia where they are chased off by soldiers and forced to jump into a lake filled with crocodiles. He then spends a year and a half with a group headed for Kenya--then America. The book is about what happens on his many attempts to escape fighting in his village.<br /><br />Things get a bid muddled though, when you flash-forward to Nya, a young African girl who is later connected to Salva in a weird ending. Nya has a good story herself, but it interrupts the main story structure, and Salvo's character falls flat in the middle, leaving some parts of the story, like of his family for instance, with loose ends, while other parts seem unrealistic. This could be befuddling for inquisitive kids (like my niece who wanted to know: "but what happened to his mommy?"). <br /><br />Great book for a child who is just learning about the impact of atrocities that children their age face around the world. The story of a Salva is a moving one. </span>
  <a data-text-id="18289041240529071694" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_128499516" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/128499516" />
    <a title="Roxanne Hsu Feldman" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/315628-roxanne-hsu-feldman"><img alt="Roxanne Hsu Feldman" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442478014p2/315628.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/128499516?book_show_action=true">Oct 29, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Roxanne Hsu Feldman" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Roxanne Hsu Feldman" href="/user/show/315628-roxanne-hsu-feldman">Roxanne Hsu Feldman</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/315628-roxanne-hsu-feldman?shelf=6-8grade">6-8grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/315628-roxanne-hsu-feldman?shelf=realisticfiction">realisticfiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer128499516" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11902228614584794249">This is a quiet book; it is also an explosive and extremely powerful book. For such a short book, it really packs a huge punch -- one that lingers in my mind and makes me want to know more, find out more, and help out if I can! <br/><br/>It is a quiet book because Park reports and does not sensationalize. At times, in the beginning of Salva's journey, I felt a slight disconnect: I did not feel that his forced exile from his village or even the loss of his new friend are scenes that moved me emotionally. A</span>
  <span id="freeText11902228614584794249" style="display:none">This is a quiet book; it is also an explosive and extremely powerful book. For such a short book, it really packs a huge punch -- one that lingers in my mind and makes me want to know more, find out more, and help out if I can! <br /><br />It is a quiet book because Park reports and does not sensationalize. At times, in the beginning of Salva's journey, I felt a slight disconnect: I did not feel that his forced exile from his village or even the loss of his new friend are scenes that moved me emotionally. As I kept reading, my mind and my heart mingled: the words that are matter-of-facts also became matter-of-heart and matter-of-wisdom. The portion of the journey involving Salva's uncle, his guidance, and his death, is the center piece of the tale. I even feel that I've learned a precious lesson from his mantra of taking one step at a time, solving one problem at a time -- to conquer seemingly insurmountable obstacles or to achieve seemingly impossible goals.<br /><br />It is a powerful book because Park manages to tell a harrowing tale to a young audience that will surely stimulate empathy and activism. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11902228614584794249" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2163609995&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2163609995" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9387071070264056760">After I read this book, I realized how sad or poor many other places in the world was. While I was at home, playing games or eating amazing food, there were people starving and dying. War. Death. Friends. There were many sad moments, but in the end, it was happy. It taught me many things, like how if you keep on trying you will succeed. Salva kept on trying, and eventually made it to both of the camps. He also kept on trying to raise money for Sudan after he got to America, and he eventually got</span>
  <span id="freeText9387071070264056760" style="display:none">After I read this book, I realized how sad or poor many other places in the world was. While I was at home, playing games or eating amazing food, there were people starving and dying. War. Death. Friends. There were many sad moments, but in the end, it was happy. It taught me many things, like how if you keep on trying you will succeed. Salva kept on trying, and eventually made it to both of the camps. He also kept on trying to raise money for Sudan after he got to America, and he eventually got to build the wells. It's really hard for me to connect to this book, as I can't connect to how much pain the people of Sudan was experiencing, but I can connect to how hard work will help you succeed. Everyone tells me this, my teachers, my parents, my friends. At first I didn't really believe it, but after I read this book I started to believe it a bit more.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer120318202" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9197149596459778814">The long civil war in Sudan destroyed the country and devastated its people. Park alternates the stories of two Sudanese children, one a Lost Boy, forced to flee his village during an attack and seek refuge in Ethiopia, and a young girl who walks for miles each day to collect water for her family. A brief, powerful story explaining the Sudanese conflict to children and one boy's hope and courage.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1397793077" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1397793077" />
    <a title="Jennifer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9420458-jennifer"><img alt="Jennifer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1494101394p2/9420458.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1397793077?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer" href="/user/show/9420458-jennifer">Jennifer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9420458-jennifer?shelf=children-s-books">children-s-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9420458-jennifer?shelf=2015-coffee-books-challenge">2015-coffee-books-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1397793077" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18084269837076919039">As a parent, I've spent a lot of time protecting my childrens' innocence about the world. We've been blessed beyond belief to live in a first world country, in a safe community, where our needs our met, where my kids have been able to be kids. Sure, they're aware of "the needy", we sponsor a child through World Vision, and they've learned about Haiti and Rwanda through some mission programs at our church. But they don't really know the details of the suffering. My older child has now reached an </span>
  <span id="freeText18084269837076919039" style="display:none">As a parent, I've spent a lot of time protecting my childrens' innocence about the world. We've been blessed beyond belief to live in a first world country, in a safe community, where our needs our met, where my kids have been able to be kids. Sure, they're aware of "the needy", we sponsor a child through World Vision, and they've learned about Haiti and Rwanda through some mission programs at our church. But they don't really know the details of the suffering. My older child has now reached an age where some of that protection needs to be turned to education. "A Long Walk to Water" is an excellent novel to do just that.<br /><br />"A Long Walk to Water" has two parallel story lines. The first, which starts in 1985, focuses on Salva, who becomes one of the Lost Boys of Sudan when his village is attacked in the middle of the school day and he must flee for safety -- a heartbreaking journey which takes years and spans countries and continents.<br /><br />The second story line starts in 2008 and focuses on Nya, a Sudanese girl whose sole activity in life is to walk miles to and from a watering hole each day to collect dirty water (the only available kind) for her family. <br /><br />The book is written for middle grade readers, so adults may find it lacking in depth and predictable. However, I think it hits the sweet spot for its intended audience. Middle grade readers will find suspense, action, and a sense of empathy for the characters in both of the story lines. My daughter was compelled to find out more about both the Lost Boys as well as access to clean water -- and I doubt she is alone. The book has given us an opportunity to discuss not only history and geography, but also better helps her understand the current Syrian refugee crisis. I highly recommend this for middle grade readers. </span>
  <a data-text-id="18084269837076919039" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2163370741" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2163370741" />
    <a title="Ian_E1" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71348414-ian-e1"><img alt="Ian_E1" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1512552151p2/71348414.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2163370741?book_show_action=true">Nov 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ian_E1" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ian_E1" href="/user/show/71348414-ian-e1">Ian_E1</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2163370741" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10544183671316720211">(A little spoiling)<br/>The book "A Long Walk to Water: Based on a True Story" was such a inspirational book that made me compare Salva's story, to mine. I have a family. I have education. I have other needs in life that Salva doesn't. It made me wonder how much things that I "want" rather than I "need". It made me wonder how much just one's help, can change someone's life. It made me wonder how not knowing things, can hurt. It made me realize how I'm too lazy to go from my room to the refrigerator t</span>
  <span id="freeText10544183671316720211" style="display:none">(A little spoiling)<br />The book "A Long Walk to Water: Based on a True Story" was such a inspirational book that made me compare Salva's story, to mine. I have a family. I have education. I have other needs in life that Salva doesn't. It made me wonder how much things that I "want" rather than I "need". It made me wonder how much just one's help, can change someone's life. It made me wonder how not knowing things, can hurt. It made me realize how I'm too lazy to go from my room to the refrigerator to get water, while half way across the world in Sudan, a country next to Ethiopia that ended a civil war not too long ago, there is someone(Nya) walking hours just to get muddy water. Not only just to get water. Going to the nearest school and medic takes hours also. Just like Nya explains, water can be the key to life. It can bring happiness to families. Peacefulness. Education. <br />Now talking about Salva and his family, he meets his father in 19 years! In nineteen years, someone can change so much to forget their son's face. I wonder when Salva met his mother and his brother. Now thinking about it, the war has also changed Salva in many ways. First and the most obvious, he was stronger after the words uncle told him. "Just one more step" "Just till the bushes over there". This and his friends death kept him going to his destination. Next, the war made Salva run away and not fight for the war. This made him go to america since he didn't fight. He also didn't get the scar on his forehead because he ran away from the war. Finally, the war shaped Salva to who he is today. Going to southern Sudan and helping people there. Even generous to face the Nuer and dig a well for them. <br />Anyways, I recommend this book to anyone. From elementary to adults. Everyone should read this book.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2170235315" />
    <a title="DanielC_C1" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71349617-danielc-c1"><img alt="DanielC_C1" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1552446324p2/71349617.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2170235315?book_show_action=true">Nov 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="DanielC_C1" class="user" itemprop="url" name="DanielC_C1" href="/user/show/71349617-danielc-c1">DanielC_C1</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2170235315" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17170078204213275243">In every book, there is always one line that is the soul of the book. Remove that one line, and the book turns to rust. This book has one of the most amazing soul-of-the-books in all the books I've read. I believe that the soul in this book is the line "Just this one step-one step at a time." This message is not only repeated, but it is also meaningful. Chinese philosopher, Lao Zi, has once said that "a journey of a thousand miles starts with a single step." These two pieces of text connect toge</span>
  <span id="freeText17170078204213275243" style="display:none">In every book, there is always one line that is the soul of the book. Remove that one line, and the book turns to rust. This book has one of the most amazing soul-of-the-books in all the books I've read. I believe that the soul in this book is the line "Just this one step-one step at a time." This message is not only repeated, but it is also meaningful. Chinese philosopher, Lao Zi, has once said that "a journey of a thousand miles starts with a single step." These two pieces of text connect together. Have you ever felt something was too big to be done? If you look at the whole thing, you would be under a lot of stress and pressure. But, if you take it one piece at a time, you would find it easier. In the book, Salva's story literally revolved around this one line. When he was walking from South Sudan to Ethiopia, he was thinking of this sentence to encourage himself. When he was running to Kenya, he was taking his days one day at a time-just this one day. When he was digging wells for the Sudanese, he was thinking of what his uncle had taught him. <br />This is a very meaningful book. Heavily recommended if you want an inspirational novel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17170078204213275243" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11855000403978555423">Own.<br/><br/>This book was very moving and thought provoking. It was a relatively short and easy read from a technical standpoint. Park did a lovely job weaving Nya and Salva's stories together. Nya's more modern story was changed by Salva's earlier experiences. The lessons of one step in front of the other and simply reaching the next plateau were well revived, time and again. It was valuable exposure to the experiences of people in our world and the challenges so many face: war, lack of access to resou</span>
  <span id="freeText11855000403978555423" style="display:none">Own.<br /><br />This book was very moving and thought provoking. It was a relatively short and easy read from a technical standpoint. Park did a lovely job weaving Nya and Salva's stories together. Nya's more modern story was changed by Salva's earlier experiences. The lessons of one step in front of the other and simply reaching the next plateau were well revived, time and again. It was valuable exposure to the experiences of people in our world and the challenges so many face: war, lack of access to resources, refugees, government unrest, etc. Park packs a lot of ideas into a slim book written for children.<br /><br />Even though this book is probably aimed more at an upper elementary age group, I found it a worthwhile read for my Middle Grade homeschool students who have been, perhaps, a little more sheltered than others their age. It was a quick read for us and I could tell there was a lot of thinking going on. While it wasn't a *fun* read, it was an important one. </span>

<div id="review_2591534770" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2591534770" />
    <a title="Angela_C1" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/85496056-angela-c1"><img alt="Angela_C1" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2591534770?book_show_action=true">Nov 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela_C1" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela_C1" href="/user/show/85496056-angela-c1">Angela_C1</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2591534770" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9924823204458469963">I think one of the important factors in the book is development. Development empowers entire Sudanese villages by giving the villagers more time for other pursuits, such as education. By installing a simple well in the middle of the village, for example, engineers save the villagers countless hours of walking—adding up to weeks or months, probably—every year. Following the same logic, this type of development empowers women: Nya, for instance, will be able to attend school alongside her male pee</span>
  <span id="freeText9924823204458469963" style="display:none">I think one of the important factors in the book is development. Development empowers entire Sudanese villages by giving the villagers more time for other pursuits, such as education. By installing a simple well in the middle of the village, for example, engineers save the villagers countless hours of walking—adding up to weeks or months, probably—every year. Following the same logic, this type of development empowers women: Nya, for instance, will be able to attend school alongside her male peers and learn how to read and write due to the time the new well saves her. No country can develop when half of its population is marginalized. <br /><br />The book also shows how development might ease cultural tensions in Sudan as a whole. Salva Dut, who initiates an influential project to build wells in Sudan, makes a point of designing wells for many different tribes, not just his own Dinka tribe. In this way, Salva makes sure that the different cultural and ethnic groups in South Sudan reap the rewards of development equally. Furthermore, the author suggests that many of the rivalries between tribes stem from disputes over access to water, meaning that providing clean water for the different tribes will make South Sudan more a more peaceful place for its inhabitants.<br /><br />I can make a text-to-world connection the South Sudanese refugee crisis and the situation Salva and Nya is in. Last week, I participated in SHASMUN VII as the delegate of South Africa. We had a variety of constructive and fruitful debates, including a debate on resolution of the South Sudanese refugee crisis. This debate further enhanced my learning on the background history and the current situation inn South Sudan. It also put me in the shoes of the UN that strived to build a better future for Nya and Salva. Furthermore, this experience relates to the political video we watched in class because the exact same thing happened in the conference. In the video, USA vetoed the resolution by the United Nations of aborting weapon transportation to South Sudan, which could possibly save thousands of lives. At the conference, Congo and Kenya submitted a clause on the s of weapon transportation, but the delegate of USA, pertaining to his country stance, vetoed it by striking the clause. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9924823204458469963" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10497663226874564689">After I read this book, I could clearly understand the theme of the book. Which I believe that it was, if you have a goal in life, as long as you try you can always accomplish it and never lose hope. I believe that that was the theme of this book because the book continuously proves to us that that is the theme of the book. The first time we see this is when Salva starts his long walking journey to safety and freedom from violence in the beginning of the book. The next major scene that we see th</span>
  <span id="freeText10497663226874564689" style="display:none">After I read this book, I could clearly understand the theme of the book. Which I believe that it was, if you have a goal in life, as long as you try you can always accomplish it and never lose hope. I believe that that was the theme of this book because the book continuously proves to us that that is the theme of the book. The first time we see this is when Salva starts his long walking journey to safety and freedom from violence in the beginning of the book. The next major scene that we see this is when Salva is on his own and is leading thousands of other boys after the event in the Ethiopian refugee camps. In this scene, we first hear Salva continuously try to get to safety with the other thousands of children. We can see Salva really trying to achieve a goal. This is different compared to the past is that this time, Salva is choosing his choices instead of another adult choosing it for him like his uncle. The final time that we see Salva showing this is when he starts the project to help both Dinka and Nuer access water easily. Donations. Speeches. Volunteers. The book specifically states that Salva spent a lot of effort to achieve his goal. All of this took years to accomplish. Throughout the book we see the book telling us that all you need to do to acheive your goal is try.</span>

  <span id="freeText13662094031586201922" style="display:none">This book is amazing. I really like how it shows different examples of life in Southern Sudan. Salva and Nya's life were so different, yet they live in the same country and same culture, it's just the time period is different. Also, I was deeply touched by, especially, Salva's courage. His life is so different then ours, and our lives are better than his in many ways, yet, he never gave up, and at the end probably experienced and learned more than we ever will. I admire him for that. Another part of the book that I really liked, was at the end, at how Nya didn't have to walk to the pond for water. Instead, she could go to school. I was really moved at this because of her enthusiasm and her wanting to learn. Because of this, she probably will understand the full meaning of going to school and getting an education, and how important it is for the future. That is why I really enjoyed reading this book, and if you haven't read it, I really recommend that you do.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13662094031586201922" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3012021603" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3012021603" />
    <a title="Maddie Smith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/98385354-maddie-smith"><img alt="Maddie Smith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568620464p2/98385354.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3012021603?book_show_action=true">Oct 14, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maddie Smith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maddie Smith" href="/user/show/98385354-maddie-smith">Maddie Smith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3012021603" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17092410631251581544"><br/>In this book, the main character, Salva, has to be very persistent. If he didn't show this trait, then he might not even survive the situation he's in. He needs to keep walking, without stopping, and he doesn't even know where he is going. All he knows is that him and his group are trying to get away from the war, anywhere where it is not.<br/>If I were in Salva's situation, I don't think I would be able to survive. He has walked for 1 whole week without stopping, he hasn't eaten hardly anything, and</span>
  <span id="freeText17092410631251581544" style="display:none"><br />In this book, the main character, Salva, has to be very persistent. If he didn't show this trait, then he might not even survive the situation he's in. He needs to keep walking, without stopping, and he doesn't even know where he is going. All he knows is that him and his group are trying to get away from the war, anywhere where it is not.<br />If I were in Salva's situation, I don't think I would be able to survive. He has walked for 1 whole week without stopping, he hasn't eaten hardly anything, and he is feeling horrible about himself because half of the group that he is traveling with wishes that they hadn't taken him with them. I would feel embarrassed and scared that if I did something wrong, the group would just leave me behind in their tracks. <br />The fact that he barely eats is horrible, but on top of that, he has to walk the whole day without eating, so he has no source of energy. And to make his situation even worse, he doesn't even know if his family is alive. They could be dead, alone, dying...he has no clue. <br />But this takes him forward. He knows that if he gives up, then he will never see his family again, even if they are alive. So he keeps pushing. Pushing to survive, pushing to show that he is worthy, pushing to make sure that he doesn't get left behind like an object that somebody left buried in the sand.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17092410631251581544" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2189600871" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2189600871" />
    <a title="Aanya_C1" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71349765-aanya-c1"><img alt="Aanya_C1" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2189600871?book_show_action=true">Nov 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aanya_C1" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aanya_C1" href="/user/show/71349765-aanya-c1">Aanya_C1</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2189600871" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2403057416200864805">A long walk to water is a novel about two stories, Salva's, and Nya's. Nya is a girl who has to fetch water every single day, from a pond miles away from her village. Salva lives in a war-zone, and believes himself to be the only survivor when the rebels attacked his village. What I liked most about the book was the determination and hope of the main protagonist, Salva. He was an orphan, a twelve year old boy who had to walk thousands of miles to different refugee camps all over East Africa, but</span>
  <span id="freeText2403057416200864805" style="display:none">A long walk to water is a novel about two stories, Salva's, and Nya's. Nya is a girl who has to fetch water every single day, from a pond miles away from her village. Salva lives in a war-zone, and believes himself to be the only survivor when the rebels attacked his village. What I liked most about the book was the determination and hope of the main protagonist, Salva. He was an orphan, a twelve year old boy who had to walk thousands of miles to different refugee camps all over East Africa, but somehow he became one of the few people who survived. He just kept thinking "I just have to make it through this day, one step at a time". My biggest connection to Salva was the feeling that he was getting too much on his plate, and he couldn't eat through it all. I get that feeling sometimes when I have too much homework, or am just stressed for some reason. I do the same thing salva does, take a deep breath and think that I just have to get through this day. Regarding the writing, I thought It was very well written, but there were some long, unnecessary parts which I thought could be cut and make the book more fast paced with less build-up. Overall, an excellent read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2403057416200864805" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('SSe6bHF+ls20FkWWwM4gbG1JdGou2Mm7uZtBfr1eDG1JwrJ4Yr1dxrtFOslXxDfkXkrCOhtWOJU2fflHEGepMw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer5044650391988733831">Linda Sue Park is a Korean American author of children's fiction. Park published her first novel, Seesaw Girl, in 1999. To date, she has written six children’s novels and five picture books for younger readers. Park’s work achieved prominence when she received the prestigious 2002 Newbery Medal for her novel A Single Shard.<br/><br/></span>
